## Page 3

REVIEW OF LOCAL GOVERNMENT BOUNDARIES
UNDER LOCAL GOVERNMENT ACT (NI) 1972
FOREWORD TO REVISED RECOMMENDATIONS
THE PROVISIONAL RECOMMENDATIONS
The provisional recommendations were published on 20 May 1983 after consideration of the 70 proposals recelved as a
result of the notice of | November 1982 published in 44 Belfast and local newspapers and the 200 odd letters sent to
district councils, government and public departments, political and trade associations, members of the Westminster
and European Parliaments, and of the Northern Ireland Assembly, Inviting such proposals.
The notices published In the Belfast and local newspapers announcing the publication of the provisional recommendations
on 20 May stated that the recommendations for Northern Ireland as a whole were being exhibited at Parliament
Buildings, Stormont; the Housing Advice Centre, Belfast; and the Guildhall, Londonderry. They also gave particulars of
the places where the recommendations for each individual district might be inspected during the period of one month
from 20 May and indicated that any representations or objections regarding the recommendations should be made in
writing not later than 20 June 1983.
The Commisstoner also gave notice that he would consider holding a public hearing in respect of certain specific issues
upon which he wished to be better informed and which were set out in paragraph 17 of the Foreword to the provisional
recommendations.
The provisional recommendations were contained In 49 maps which showed both the existing and the provisionally
recommended ward and district boundaries, with their respective names.
The maps expressed the definitive recommendations, as It was Intended when the provisional recommendations came
to be revised, and later when final recommendations have to be made, that the recommendations should be in the form
of maps setting out the boundaries and names for districts and their wards. To facilitate identification of the
townlands, streets etc within each ward, an ancillary text has been added for ease of reference.
THE REPRESENTATIONS AND OBJECTIONS
3 Representations and objections in writing, many of a composite nature, were recelved In respect of the provisional
recommendations from a total of 74 sources Including councils, elected representatives and political parties, individuals
and other bodies, and all such representations have been taken into account In making the revised recommendations.
The Commissioner decided to hold public hearings within 19 districts, that is in all bute 7 districts, namely Ards.
Ballymoney, Carrickfergus, Larne. Londonderry, Newry and Mourne and Strabane. The hearings covered not only
matters which had been represented to him, but also issues upon which he required assistance from or on behalf of the
electors who were affected by his provisional recommendations.
All hearings were advertised In the Belfast and local newspapers and were held between 31 August and [7 November
[983 (Inclusive).
Every representation or objection received was acknowledged and where it was made In general terms, or lacked
sufficient particulars to define the subject matter fully, the person or body concerned was given the opportunity to
amplify that representation; and where a public hearing was to be held the need for early submission of the full
particulars of what was to be represented at that hearing was explained.

## Page 4

ASSISTANT COMMISSIONERS
The Commissioner was assisted throughout the public hearings by three Assistant Commissioners, namely Mr§ FR Martin
Mr K ] Donaghy and Mr J P McGrath who sat with him In turn, and who in his absence conducted the hearings for
Ballymena, Moyle and North Down. The function of the Assistant Commissioners was to assess the content and Welghe
of the representations made, and to exercise independent judgement so as to advise the Commissioner whether or nor
4.
to revise what he had provisionally recommended.
It must be recorded that in considering the repesentations the Assistant Commissioners played an active and important
role: and in making the revised recommendations now published, there is no revision recommended, which does not
have the support of the Assistant Commissioners.
THE PUBLIC HEARINGS
One matter requires special mention. The public notices and the Foreword to the provisional recommendations required 5.
that any representation or objection regarding what was recommended provisonally should be made in writing not :
later than Monday, 20 June 1983.
Paragraph 2! of the Foreword also stated that “The fact that no representation has been made in writing will not
necessarily preclude any person from taking part In the hearing In respect of issues which have been raised by a
representation or objection duly made by another party”.
The intention of this paragraph was to convey the general message that not only what the Commissioner had provisionally
recommended would be considered at the relevant public hearing but also that every representation or objection
“duly made”, chat Is to say In writing by 20 June, could be tested at the hearing by anyone interested In the Issues raised
thereby.
Nevertheless at several public hearings persons on behalf of associations with political objects appeared and made verbal
representations supported by maps or texts of townlands and streets proposing alternative patterns for wards within the
relevance district, without having given notice in writing of any such intention either by 20 June or at any time before
appearing at the public hearing.
Each of these representations purported to object to the provisional recommendations for the district by proposing
substantive changes which were in such general terms that the exact boundaries of the wards proposed and the precise
electorates which would result from the alternative pattern were left uncertain
The general proposition made In most of these cases was that the number of wards provisionally recommended would
result in under-representation for rural areas and, comparing one district with another, that there was no uniformity
as to the electorates In rural areas. It was also sald that there was a disparity between the rural and urban electorates
in many districts. The degree of under-representation alleged was generally by one or possibly two wards, except in
Fermanagh where an increase of 6 or 7 additional wards over the existing 20 was sought by several political bodies.
Objection by persons appearing was taken to the consideration of these late alternative proposals on the grounds eal
(f) che public hearings were for che purpose of examining the provisional recommendations. and not alternative
patterns for wards;
Q) the alternative patterns were not sufficiently precise to allow full examination at the public hearing:
(3) there was Insufficient opportunity for parties and persons Opposing an alternative pattern to study and resist
what was proposed; and that
(4) the Commissioner had no statutory power to consider such alternative proposals at the stage of a public
hearing which was to consider his own provisional recommendations

## Page 5

Notwithstanding the late submission at the public hearings of what constituted substantive proposals for ward changes
and which were incompletely worked out as regards the definition of ward boundaries and their electorates within the
particular district, the Commissioner decided to examine each of these proposals as a means of testing the validity
of his own provisional recommendations, and has done so in each case. This involved working out, as best could be done,
more exact boundaries and electorates from proposals which were Inexact and therefore to some extent speculative.
In the event, he Is firmly of the view that the case for under-representation has not been made out, as an
a examination of the Schedule to the Foreword will show. Inter alia, che Schedule displays In ascending order the
electorates under the revised recommendations for districts and their electorates, and also the average electorate in the
“middle 14 districts” which for this purpose leaves out of account the smaller and larger districts.
The Schedule Is Included for those who wish to make such comparisons, but the Commissioner's approach to the
problem has not been to start from such simple arithmetical comparisons, but instead has been to consider how many
distinct urban, village or rural communities are present within a particular boundary for a particular district,
and then to consider how to achieve a ward pattern which would allow proper representation for those communities
within the requirement of broadly equivalent electorates. And whether this approach, which is based on social
and dernographic factors, Is successful can only be judged by its results, and though too much should not be read
out of the fact, It is not Insignificant that, before the public hearings commenced, no Council had said that the
1972 pattern for its wards, and their electorates, had proved inadequate for proper representation over the last
10 years, and a number of Councils with largely rural electorates wanted no increase in che number of wards.
ELECTORAL EQUIVALENCE
6. The difficulty of creating wards which have recognisable local identities while maintaining the principle of equivalent
electorates has been largely met by allowing a tolerance of 10% over or under the average district electorates and this
degree of tolerance has only been departed from in a few cases where the Council, or a preponderence of local feeling,
' has indicated willingness to accept a ward electorate above or below this tolerance.
Many representations were based on counting electorates as they appear In the 1983 Register, but the 1972 Act
requires the Commissioner to base his recommendations upon the register of local electors in force when he commenced
his task on | November 1982.
ELECTORAL AREAS
7. The misconception regarding the Commissioner's statutory function was carried into the representations and Into the
submissions made at the public hearings, so that in many cases the express or implied basis for proposing the rejection
or alteration of the provisional recommendations was the expectation that the grouping of wards into electoral areas
could thereby be influenced.
No doubt changes in the composition of wards may be viewed by political Interests according to how wards may be
grouped into electoral areas for the purpose of proportional representation, but this is a later, and different exercise
from that with which the Commissioner {s charged. He has made it plain that his review was not directed to the creation
of electoral areas, and that his aim was the creation of wards which are coherent social units with electorates broadly
equivalent within each district as far as geographical and local identities permitted, and further that he was not
advised as to the form which such electoral groupings might take.
Since the revised maps were completed for printing, the District Electoral Areas Commissioner Order has been laid
before Parllament on 15 December 1983 and, if approved, It will provide the means by which the wards recommended
by the Local Government Boundaries Commissioner can be grouped for electoral purposes and will establish the
procedures under which representations may be made in respect of the proposed groupings.

## Page 6

THE REVISED RECOMMENDATIONS
8. The revised recommendations for Northern Ireland as a whole are presented in the form of 52 maps. They show
where the district and ward boundaries depart from the provisional
d names are not indicated.
recommendations, although, where ward nameg
have been revised the provisionally recommende
The revised recommendations provide for several alterations in district boundaries which when added to earlier change
proposed at the provisional scage would have the effect of altering the present boundaries of 7 districts.
PARLIAMENTARY BOUNDARIES
9. Attention was directed in the Foreword to the provisional recommendations to the circumstances that the *
Commissioner's final recommendations, with or without modifications, will not, when enacted, affect either Parliamentary
or Assembly constituencies as these boundaries under existing legislation are based upon the local government districts
and their wards as constituted by the Local Government (Boundarles) Order (NI) 1972. It was pointed out at the
public hearings by many persons of differing political views that this results in confusing electors partly because they
may have to go to different polling stations for different elections but more importantly because neighbours with
commen social problems within the same local government district will have to resort to different Assembly and
Parliamentary members where local government boundaries are not coincident with Assembly and Parliamentary
constituencies. Coincidence between boundaries for constituencies at different levels of government would seem
to have obvious advantages for the electorate, but the statutory powers given to the Commissioner cannot be
applied to this end, and the most that he can do in making his revised recommendations Is to propose changes
in local government boundaries which breach other constituency boundaries only where the case for such change is
strongly made out on social and demographic grounds. Though it will be found chat there are quite a
substantial number of such revisions recommended which have this effect, many involve only relatively small numbers
of electors.
THE NEXT STAGE
10. The notices already published in the Belfast and local press indicate where the revised recommendations for Northern
lreland as a whole and for individual districts are being displayed, and also state that representations may be made
in writing regarding the revised recommendations not later than Friday, 17 February 1984. The Commissioner wishes
to emphasise that they must be received by this date.
In addition to the public notices, over 200 letters have been sent to district councils, government and public departments,
political parties and members of the Westminster and European Parliaments and of the Northern Ireland Assembly.
These letters have stressed that representations proposing a change in any boundary should give particular and reasonable
definition of what Is proposed and indicate what change would result in the electorates affected.
The Commlssioner is not obliged to hold any public hearing following representations concerning his revised
recommendations, but he will consider every such submission closely and critically and will, if he considers that any such
submission requires scrutiny In public, hold a public hearing in respect of the revised recommendations for the relevant
district.
The purpose of any such public hearing will be to consider the recommendations as revised with a view to achieving
improvement in the pattern of revised wards. lt would not be the Commission's intention to conduct a re-hearing of
arguments already advanced, and the object would be to achieve greater community identification in conjunction with
electoral equivalence in the wards within the distrtict,

## Page 7

In view of the representations made at the public hearings held in respect of the provisional recommendations
particularly in Fermanagh and Banbridge districts, any further representations in writing regarding the revised
recommendations for those districts and In any other case for which a public hearing Is sought, should be of a sufficient
degree of particularity to be readily understandable by any person or body concerned elther to support or oppose such
representations. A public hearing Is useful to the extent that the public concerned can understand and express
views on what Is being represented to the Commissioner.
THE FINAL STAGE
I. When all representations in writing have been considered together with any submissions made at any further public
hearings, the Commissioner will submit to the Department of the Environment for Northern Ireland a report of his final
recommendations regarding the number, boundaries and names of districts and thelr wards. Subsequently, as required
by section 50(4) of the 1972 Act, statutory effect will be given, whether with or without modifications, to the
recommendations.
APPENDIX
[2 A table of general information concerning area, population, rateable value, the number of wards recommended, etc Is
given in the appendix.

## Page 13

REVISED RECOMMENDATIONS FOR LOCAL
GOVERNMENT DISTRICT OF LONDONDERRY:
DECEMBER 1983
I. It is recommended that the boundary and the name of the district, established by
the Local Government (Boundaries) Order (NI) 1972, shall remain unchanged, as
shown on the district map (Sheet |).
2. The 1972 Order also provided that the district comprise 27 wards. It is now
recommended that the district consist of 30 wards, as shown on the district
map (Sheet |) and — the urban map of Londonderry (Sheet | and Sheet 2).
The names and compositions of the 30 wards are as follows:
|. BANAGHER
The townlands of Alcaghoney, Altinure Lower, Altinure Upper, Ballyhanedin, Ballyrory, Binn, Carnanbane, Carnanreagh, Clagan,
Coolnacolpagh, Dreen, Dunady, Eden, Gilky Hill, Gortscreagan, Kilcreen, Kilculmagrandal, Kilgort, Killycor, Kinculbrack, Lear,
Letterlogher, Ling, Lisbunny, Loughtilube, Moneyhoghan, Sallowilly, Straid, Tamnagh, Teenaght, Terrydreen, Tireighter, Tirglassan,
Tullintrain, Umrycam and Dungorkin and part of Mulderg as shown on the district map (Sheet |) as part of the ward.
2. CLAUDY
The townlands of Ardground, Ardkill, Ballyartan, Ballycallaghan, Ballyholly, Ballymaclanigan, Barr Cregg, Brackfield, Claudy, Cregg,
Cumber, Ervey, Glasakeeran, Glenlough, Gortilea, Gortnaran, Gortnaskey, Gosheden, Kilcaltan, Kildoag, Killatoo, Knockbrack,
Lackagh, Legaghory, Legavannon, Lettermire, Lettermuck, Lisdillon, Listress, Lower Alla, Monehanegan, Oughtagh, Raspberry Hill,
Slaghtmanus, Strathall, Tamnymore, Toneduff and Upper Alla and part of Mulderg as shown on the district map (Sheet |) as part
of the ward.
3. EGLINTON
The townlands of Ballygroll, Ballygudden, Black Brae (Intake), Brockagh, Carmoney, Carnakilly Lower, Carnakilly Upper,
Clanterkee, Clonmakane, Coolafinny, £ralgbrack, Derryarkin Upper, Donnybrewer, Donnybrewer Level (Intake), Drummaneny,
Edenreagh Beg, Edenreagh More, Falloward, Fallowlea, Gortenny, Gortinreid, Highmoor, Laraghaleas, Longfield Level (Intake),
Longfield More, Lower Campsey, Lower Derryarkin, Lower Gortagherty, McLean and Partners Division, Monnaboy, Muff,
Mullaboy, Oghill, Sale Works, Tamnaherin, Tamnyreagh, Templemoyle, Tullanee, Tully, Tygore, Upper Campsey, Upper
Gortagherty and Whitehill and also islands in the sea where lying within the extension of the ward boundaries.

## Page 14

4. NEW BUILDINGS
Primity, Kittybane. Dunhugh, Prehen and Brickkilns and part of Bolies: and including Dunhugh Park
The townlands of Ballyore,
Summer Hill, Greenwood Avenue, Sandringham Drive, Riversdale Road, Ravens
Prehen Park, lveagh Park, Woodland Drive.
Park, Knoxhill Avenue, Sunningdale Drive, Dunnwood Park, Woodside Park, Foyle Crescent, Primity Crescent, Primity Gardens
Primity Terrace, Rock Park, Silverbrook Park, Ballyore Drive and Carrowreagh Park and parts of Prehen Road, Victoria Road
Gortinure Road and Duncastle Road and that part of the River Foyle as shown on the urban map of Londonderry (Sheet 2) as
part of the ward.
5. CORRODY
The townlands of Carnafarn. Lisglass, Drumconan, Disertowen, Upper Tully, Tagharina, Killymallaght, Tirkeeveny, Craigtown,
Drumagore, Curryfree, Creevedonnell, Lower Tully, Clampernow, Gortin, Rossnagalliagh, Magheracanon, Greerstown or Cloghore,
Gortinure, Glenderowen, Warbleshinny, Gortgranagh, Clondermot, Upper Tullyally, Corrody, Cromkill, Lower Tullyally and
Tamnymore (Londonderry) and parts of Gobnascale (Londonderry), Lisaghmore or The Trench and Bolies; and including HilWiew

1] REVISED RECOMMENDATIONS FOR LOCAL
1} GOVERNMENT DISTRICT OF LIMAVADY:
1} DECEMBER 1983
lt is recommended that the boundary and the name of the district, established by
the Local Government (Boundaries) Order (NI) [972, shall remain unchanged, as
shown on the district map.
The 1972 Order also provided that the district comprise 15 wards. It is
recommended that the number of wards shall remain unchanged but that
all the ward boundaries and some ward names shall be changed, as shown
on the district map and the urban maps of Limavady and Dungiven. The
names and compositions of the [5 wards are as follows:

l. It ls recommended that the boundary and the name of the district, established by

shown on the district map.

REVISED RECOMMENDATIONS FOR LOCAL
GOVERNMENT DISTRICT OF FERMANAGH:
DECEMBER 1983
l. It is recommended that the boundary and the name of the district, established by
the Local Government (Boundaries) Order (NI) 1972, shall remain unchanged, as
shown on the district maps (Sheets | and 2).
2. The 1972 Order also provided that the district comprise 20 wards. It is now
recommended that the district shall consist of 23 wards, as shown on the district
maps (Sheets | and 2) and the urban maps of Kesh (Sheet |) and Enniskillen and
Lisnaskea (Sheet 3). The names and compositions of the 23 wards are as follows.
|. ROSSLEA

|. It Is recommended that the boundary and the name of the district, established by
the Local Government (Boundaries) Order (NI) 1972, shall remain unchanged, as shown on the district map (Sheet 1). ;
-_
2. The 1972 Order also provided that the district comprise 20 wards. It is now
recommended that the district shall consist of 22 wards, as shown on the district
map (Sheet |) and the urban maps of Dungannon and Coalisland (Sheet 2).
The names and compositions of the 22 wards are as follows:

*EVISED RECOMMENDATIONS FOR LOCAL GOVERNMENT DISTRICT OF CRAIGAVON:
cCEMBER 1983 Te!
a
It is recommended that the. name of the district, established by the Local
Government (Boundaries) Order (NI) 1972, shall remain unchanged, but that the
boundary shall be changed, as shown on the district map (Sheet /).
2 The 1972 Order also provided that the district comprise 25 wards. It is now
recommended that the district shall consist of 26 wards, as shown on the district
map (Sheet |) and the urban maps of Portadown (Sheet |) and Craigavon and
Lurgan (Sheet 2). The names and compositions of the 26 wards are as follows:

REVISED RECOMMENDATIONS FOR LOCAL
| GOVERNMENT DISTRICT OF NEWRY & MOURNE:
| DECEMBER 1983
It Is recommended that the boundary and the name of the district, established by
the Local Government (Boundaries) Order (NI) 1972, shall remain unchanged, as
shown on the district map (Sheet |).
rw
2. The 1972 Order also provided that the district comprise 30 wards. It is
recommended that the number of the wards remain unchanged but that some
ward boundaries and names shall be changed, as shown on the district
map (Sheet |) and the urban maps of Newry and Bessbrook, Kilkee! and
Warrenpoint (Sheet 2).The names and compositions of the 30 wards
are as follows.

boundaries.

l. It is recommended that the name of the district, established by the Local Government (Boundaries) Order (NI) 1972, shall remain unchanged, but that the boundary shall be changed, as shown on the district map (Sheet |).
2. The 1972 Order also provided that the district comprise 23 wards. It is now
recommended that the district consist of 28 wards, as shown on the district
map (Sheet |) and on the urban map of Lisburn (Sheets | and 2). The names and
compositions of the 28 wards are as follows:

l. It is recommended that the boundary and the name of the district, established by
the Local Government (Boundaries) Order (NI) 1972, shall remain unchanged, as
shown on the district map.
2. The 1972 Order also provided that the district comprise 15 wards. It is
recommended that the number of wards shall remain unchanged but that some
ward boundaries and some ward names shall be changed, as shown on the
district map and the urban maps of Carrickfergus and Whitehead. The names and
compositions of the |5 wards are as follows:

REVISED RECOMMENDATIONS FOR LOCAL : GOVERNMENT DISTRICT OF BELFAST: : | DECEMBER 1983
|. It is recommended that the name of the district, established by the Local
Government (Boundaries) Order (NI) 1972, shall remain unchanged, but that the
boundary shall be changed as shown on the district map (Sheet [).
2. The 1972 Order also provided that the district comprise 51 wards. It is
recommended that the number of the wards shall remain unchanged but that
all ward boundaries and some ward names shall be changed, as shown on the
district map (Sheet |) and the urban maps (Sheets 2 to 5) of Belfast. The names
and compositions of the 51 wards are as follows.
|. SYDENHAM
The townlands of Sydenham Intake and Victoria Park and parts of Ballymaghan, Ballymisert and Strandtown; and including Colvil
Street, Connsbrook Drive, Connsbrook Park, Denorrton Park, Devon Drive, Devon Parade, Fernvale Street, Hillfoot Streec, Hill's
Avenue, inverary Avenue, Inverary Drive, Inveresk Parade, Inverleith Drive, Invernook Park, Inverwood Court, Inverwood
Gardens, Kimona Drive, Kimona Street, Kyle Sereet, Larkfield Drive, Larkfield Gardens, Larkfield Park, Larkfield Road, Lisavon
Drive, Lisavon Parade, Lisavon Street, Oakdene Drive, Oakdene Parade, Palmerston Park, Palmerston Road, Sandbrook Gardens,
Sandbrook Grove, Sandbrook Park, Sefton Drive, Sefton Park, Shaw Street, Station Road, Strand Court, Scrandburn Crescent,
Strandburn Drive, Strandburn Gardens, Strandburn Parade, Strandburn Park, Strandburn Street, Sydenham Crescent, Sydenham
Gardens, Sydenham Park, Victoria Avenue, Victoria Drive, Victoria Road, Vidor Gardens and Wellwood Avenue and parts of
Sydenham By-pass, Connsbrook Avenue, Holywood Road, Pim’s Avenue and Park Avenue and that part of Belfast Lough as
shown on the urban maps of Belfast (Sheets 2 to 5) as part of the ward.
2. ISLAND
The townlands of Queen’s Island and Ballymacarret Intake and parts of Strandtown, Ballyhackamore and Ballymacarret; and
including Alrport Road, Airport Road West, Armitage Street, Avon Street, Banbury Street, Carew Street, Chadolly Street,
Chater Street, Chelsea Street, Cuming Road, Connswater Street, Connsbank Road, Dalton Street, Dee Street, Derwent Street,
Downpatrick Street, Fern Street, Frome Street, Gawn Street, Hamilton Road, Harkness Parade, Harland Road, Humber Street,
Ina Street, Julia Street, Lelia Street, Medway Court, Medway Street, Macart Road, Musgrave Channel Road, Meekin Street,
Mersey Street, Middiepath Street, Newcastle Street, Oval Street, Pansy Street, Parkgate Crescent, Parkgate Drive, Parkgate
Gardens, Parkgate Parade, Queens Road, Queens Quay Road, Queens Quay, Redcliffe Drive, Redcliffe Parade, Redcliffe Street,
